# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`

# Task: Implement PolicyAuditLogger for Cilium

## Objective
Create a `PolicyAuditLogger` in `pkg/policy/` that provides structured logging of policy
evaluation decisions for audit and debugging purposes.

## Requirements

1. **Create `pkg/policy/audit_logger.go`** with:
   - `PolicyAuditLogger` struct with configurable log level and output
   - `LogDecision(identity, policy, verdict, reason)` method
   - `LogEvaluation(ctx, policyKey, selectorCache, result)` method
   - Integration with Cilium's existing logging framework (logrus/scopedLog)
   - Support for JSON-structured audit log output

2. **Create `pkg/policy/audit_logger_test.go`** with tests

3. **Follow Cilium patterns**:
   - Use `logfields` package for structured log fields
   - Follow the `SelectorCache` interaction pattern
   - Use `lock.Mutex` from `pkg/lock/` for thread safety

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/policy/distillery.go` — policy decision evaluation
- `pkg/policy/selectorcache.go` — SelectorCache for identity matching
- `pkg/policy/types.go` — policy types and interfaces
- `pkg/logging/logfields/logfields.go` — structured log field constants
- `pkg/lock/lock.go` — Cilium's lock primitives

## Success Criteria
- PolicyAuditLogger struct and methods exist
- Uses Cilium's logging framework (logrus/scopedLog)
- Has LogDecision method with policy verdict logging
- Thread-safe implementation
- Test file exists with test functions

  "content": "// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0\n// Copyright Authors of Cilium\n\npackage policy\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"encoding/json\"\n\n\t\"github.com/sirupsen/logrus\"\n\n\t\"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/identity\"\n\t\"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/lock\"\n\t\"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/logging/logfields\"\n)\n\n// PolicyAuditLogger provides structured logging of policy evaluation decisions\n// for audit and debugging purposes.\ntype PolicyAuditLogger struct {\n\tlock.Mutex\n\tlogger   *logrus.Logger\n\tlogLevel logrus.Level\n\tenabled  bool\n}\n\n// PolicyDecision represents a policy evaluation decision to be logged\ntype PolicyDecision struct {\n\tIdentity   identity.NumericIdentity `json:\"identity\"`\n\tPolicyName string                   `json:\"policy_name\"`\n\tVerdict    string                   `json:\"verdict\"`\n\tReason     string                   `json:\"reason\"`\n}\n\n// PolicyEvaluationResult represents the result of a policy evaluation\ntype PolicyEvaluationResult struct {\n\tPolicyKey     string `json:\"policy_key\"`\n\tSelected      bool   `json:\"selected\"`\n\tNumIdentities int    `json:\"num_identities\"`\n\tResult        string `json:\"result\"`\n}\n\n// NewPolicyAuditLogger creates a new PolicyAuditLogger with the specified logger\n// and log level.\nfunc NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger *logrus.Logger, level logrus.Level) *PolicyAuditLogger {\n\treturn &PolicyAuditLogger{\n\t\tlogger:   logger,\n\t\tlogLevel: level,\n\t\tenabled:  true,\n\t}\n}\n\n// SetLogLevel configures the log level for the audit logger\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\tpal.logLevel = level\n}\n\n// SetEnabled controls whether audit logging is enabled\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetEnabled(enabled bool) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\tpal.enabled = enabled\n}\n\n// LogDecision logs a policy decision with the provided identity, policy name,\n// verdict, and reason. This is used for audit purposes to track why specific\n// policy decisions were made.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(identity identity.NumericIdentity, policyName, verdict, reason string) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\tif !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tdecision := PolicyDecision{\n\t\tIdentity:   identity,\n\t\tPolicyName: policyName,\n\t\tVerdict:    verdict,\n\t\tReason:     reason,\n\t}\n\n\tscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n\t\tlogfields.Identity:  identity,\n\t\tlogfields.PolicyKey: policyName,\n\t\t\"verdict\":           verdict,\n\t\t\"reason\":            reason,\n\t})\n\n\t// Log the decision in structured format\n\tscopedLog.WithField(\"audit_decision\", json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(decision))).\n\t\tLogf(pal.logLevel, \"Policy decision\")\n}\n\n// LogEvaluation logs the evaluation of a policy selector against identities\n// in the SelectorCache. This tracks which identities are selected by a policy\n// and the outcome of the evaluation.\nfunc (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, policyKey string, selectorCache *SelectorCache, result bool) {\n\tpal.Lock()\n\tdefer pal.Unlock()\n\n\tif !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// Get the number of selected identities from the cache\n\tnumIdentities := 0\n\tif selectorCache != nil {\n\t\t// Count identities in the selector cache\n\t\tnumIdentities = selectorCache.numIdentities()\n\t}\n\n\tevalResult := PolicyEvaluationResult{\n\t\tPolicyKey:     policyKey,\n\t\tSelected:      result,\n\t\tNumIdentities: numIdentities,\n\t\tResult:        evalResultString(result),\n\t}\n\n\tscopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n\t\tlogfields.PolicyKey: policyKey,\n\t\t\"selected\":          result,\n\t\t\"num_identities\":    numIdentities,\n\t})\n\n\t// Log the evaluation result in structured format\n\tscopedLog.WithField(\"audit_evaluation\", json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(evalResult))).\n\t\tLogf(pal.logLevel, \"Policy evaluation\")\n}\n\n// numIdentities returns the count of identities in the SelectorCache\nfunc (sc *SelectorCache) numIdentities() int {\n\tif sc == nil {\n\t\treturn 0\n\t}\n\tsc.mutex.RLock()\n\tdefer sc.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn len(sc.idCache)\n}\n\n// evalResultString converts a boolean evaluation result to a string representation\nfunc evalResultString(result bool) string {\n\tif result {\n\t\treturn \"selected\"\n\t}\n\treturn \"not_selected\"\n}\n\n// mustMarshalJSON marshals a value to JSON, panicking if marshaling fails.\n// This is appropriate for audit logging where data integrity is critical.\nfunc mustMarshalJSON(v interface{}) []byte {\n\tdata, err := json.Marshal(v)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t// This should never happen in practice, but we panic to catch\n\t\t// logic errors during development\n\t\tpanic(\"failed to marshal audit log entry: \" + err.Error())\n\t}\n\treturn data\n}\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/pkg/policy/audit_logger.go
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
// Copyright Authors of Cilium

package policy

import (
	"context"
	"encoding/json"

	"github.com/sirupsen/logrus"

	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/identity"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/lock"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/logging/logfields"
)

// PolicyAuditLogger provides structured logging of policy evaluation decisions
// for audit and debugging purposes.
type PolicyAuditLogger struct {
	lock.Mutex
	logger   *logrus.Logger
	logLevel logrus.Level
	enabled  bool
}

// PolicyDecision represents a policy evaluation decision to be logged
type PolicyDecision struct {
	Identity   identity.NumericIdentity `json:"identity"`
	PolicyName string                   `json:"policy_name"`
	Verdict    string                   `json:"verdict"`
	Reason     string                   `json:"reason"`
}

// PolicyEvaluationResult represents the result of a policy evaluation
type PolicyEvaluationResult struct {
	PolicyKey     string `json:"policy_key"`
	Selected      bool   `json:"selected"`
	NumIdentities int    `json:"num_identities"`
	Result        string `json:"result"`
}

// NewPolicyAuditLogger creates a new PolicyAuditLogger with the specified logger
// and log level.
func NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger *logrus.Logger, level logrus.Level) *PolicyAuditLogger {
	return &PolicyAuditLogger{
		logger:   logger,
		logLevel: level,
		enabled:  true,
	}
}

// SetLogLevel configures the log level for the audit logger
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetLogLevel(level logrus.Level) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()
	pal.logLevel = level
}

// SetEnabled controls whether audit logging is enabled
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) SetEnabled(enabled bool) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()
	pal.enabled = enabled
}

... (truncated)

import (
	"bytes"
	"context"

// TestNewPolicyAuditLogger tests creating a new PolicyAuditLogger
func TestNewPolicyAuditLogger(t *testing.T) {
	logger := logrus.New()
	level := logrus.InfoLevel

	pal := NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger, level)

	require.NotNil(t, pal)
	require.Equal(t, logger, pal.logger)
	require.Equal(t, level, pal.logLevel)
	require.True(t, pal.enabled)
}

// TestSetLogLevel tests setting the log level
func TestSetLogLevel(t *testing.T) {
	logger := logrus.New()
	pal := NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger, logrus.InfoLevel)

	require.Equal(t, logrus.InfoLevel, pal.logLevel)

	pal.SetLogLevel(logrus.DebugLevel)
	require.Equal(t, logrus.DebugLevel, pal.logLevel)

	pal.SetLogLevel(logrus.WarnLevel)
	require.Equal(t, logrus.WarnLevel, pal.logLevel)
}

// TestSetEnabled tests enabling and disabling the audit logger
func TestSetEnabled(t *testing.T) {
	logger := logrus.New()
	pal := NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger, logrus.InfoLevel)

	require.True(t, pal.enabled)

	pal.SetEnabled(false)
	require.False(t, pal.enabled)

	pal.SetEnabled(true)
	require.True(t, pal.enabled)
}

// TestLogDecision tests logging a policy decision
func TestLogDecision(t *testing.T) {
	logger := logrus.New()
	buffer := &bytes.Buffer{}
	logger.SetOutput(buffer)
	logger.SetFormatter(&logrus.JSONFormatter{})
	logger.SetLevel(logrus.InfoLevel)

	pal := NewPolicyAuditLogger(logger, logrus.InfoLevel)

	testID := identity.NumericIdentity(1000)
	policyName := "test-policy"
	verdict := "allow"
	reason := "matched ingress rule"

	pal.LogDecision(testID, policyName, verdict, reason)

3. EDIT /workspace/pkg/policy/audit_logger.go
Before
// LogDecision logs a policy decision with the provided identity, policy name,
// verdict, and reason. This is used for audit purposes to track why specific
// policy decisions were made.
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(identity identity.NumericIdentity, policyName, verdict, reason string) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()

	if !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {
		return
	}

	decision := PolicyDecision{
		Identity:   identity,
		PolicyName: policyName,
		Verdict:    verdict,
		Reason:     reason,
	}

	scopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{
		logfields.Identity:  identity,
		logfields.PolicyKey: policyName,
		"verdict":           verdict,
		"reason":            reason,
	})

	// Log the decision in structured format
	scopedLog.WithField("audit_decision", json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(decision))).
		Logf(pal.logLevel, "Policy decision")
}
After
// LogDecision logs a policy decision with the provided identity, policy name,
// verdict, and reason. This is used for audit purposes to track why specific
// policy decisions were made.
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogDecision(identity identity.NumericIdentity, policyName, verdict, reason string) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()

	if !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {
		return
	}

	decision := PolicyDecision{
		Identity:   identity,
		PolicyName: policyName,
		Verdict:    verdict,
		Reason:     reason,
	}

	scopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{
		logfields.Identity:  identity,
		logfields.PolicyKey: policyName,
		"verdict":           verdict,
		"reason":            reason,
		"audit_decision":    json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(decision)),
	})

	// Log the decision in structured format
	logAtLevel(scopedLog, pal.logLevel, "Policy decision")
}
4. EDIT /workspace/pkg/policy/audit_logger.go
Before
// LogEvaluation logs the evaluation of a policy selector against identities
// in the SelectorCache. This tracks which identities are selected by a policy
// and the outcome of the evaluation.
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, policyKey string, selectorCache *SelectorCache, result bool) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()

	if !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {
		return
	}

	// Get the number of selected identities from the cache
	numIdentities := 0
	if selectorCache != nil {
		// Count identities in the selector cache
		numIdentities = selectorCache.numIdentities()
	}

	evalResult := PolicyEvaluationResult{
		PolicyKey:     policyKey,
		Selected:      result,
		NumIdentities: numIdentities,
		Result:        evalResultString(result),
	}

	scopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{
		logfields.PolicyKey: policyKey,
		"selected":          result,
		"num_identities":    numIdentities,
	})

	// Log the evaluation result in structured format
	scopedLog.WithField("audit_evaluation", json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(evalResult))).
		Logf(pal.logLevel, "Policy evaluation")
}
After
// LogEvaluation logs the evaluation of a policy selector against identities
// in the SelectorCache. This tracks which identities are selected by a policy
// and the outcome of the evaluation.
func (pal *PolicyAuditLogger) LogEvaluation(ctx context.Context, policyKey string, selectorCache *SelectorCache, result bool) {
	pal.Lock()
	defer pal.Unlock()

	if !pal.enabled || !pal.logger.IsLevelEnabled(pal.logLevel) {
		return
	}

	// Get the number of selected identities from the cache
	numIdentities := 0
	if selectorCache != nil {
		// Count identities in the selector cache
		numIdentities = selectorCache.numIdentities()
	}

	evalResult := PolicyEvaluationResult{
		PolicyKey:     policyKey,
		Selected:      result,
		NumIdentities: numIdentities,
		Result:        evalResultString(result),
	}

	scopedLog := pal.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{
		logfields.PolicyKey: policyKey,
		"selected":          result,
		"num_identities":    numIdentities,
		"audit_evaluation":  json.RawMessage(mustMarshalJSON(evalResult)),
	})

	// Log the evaluation result in structured format
	logAtLevel(scopedLog, pal.logLevel, "Policy evaluation")
}

Before
// mustMarshalJSON marshals a value to JSON, panicking if marshaling fails.
// This is appropriate for audit logging where data integrity is critical.
func mustMarshalJSON(v interface{}) []byte {
	data, err := json.Marshal(v)
	if err != nil {
		// This should never happen in practice, but we panic to catch
		// logic errors during development
		panic("failed to marshal audit log entry: " + err.Error())
	}
	return data
}
After
// mustMarshalJSON marshals a value to JSON, panicking if marshaling fails.
// This is appropriate for audit logging where data integrity is critical.
func mustMarshalJSON(v interface{}) []byte {
	data, err := json.Marshal(v)
	if err != nil {
		// This should never happen in practice, but we panic to catch
		// logic errors during development
		panic("failed to marshal audit log entry: " + err.Error())
	}
	return data
}

// logAtLevel logs a message at the specified logrus level
func logAtLevel(entry *logrus.Entry, level logrus.Level, msg string) {
	switch level {
	case logrus.DebugLevel:
		entry.Debug(msg)
	case logrus.InfoLevel:
		entry.Info(msg)
	case logrus.WarnLevel:
		entry.Warn(msg)
	case logrus.ErrorLevel:
		entry.Error(msg)
	case logrus.FatalLevel:
		entry.Fatal(msg)
	case logrus.PanicLevel:
		entry.Panic(msg)
	default:
		entry.Info(msg)
	}
}
